    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_46839b60-e010-4477-9a43-822684589b6d'

  <span id="freeText14792678537051908343" style="display:none">Reed Brennan's future is looking as bright as the two-karat diamonds in her new housemates' ears. Being accepted to the most prestigious private boarding school in the country wasn't enough for Reed. She had to break every rule to do it, but she has accomplished the impossible: <br /><br />Reed is a Billings Girl now. <br /><br />And with her new status come respect, envy, and, most important, opportunity. Not to mention the parties. Unfortunately, at the next illicit party in the Easton campus woods, her roommate snaps some pictures of Reed in more than one compromising position. She uses the photos to blackmail Reed: Dig up dirt on the most powerful and popular Billings Girls or she will have Reed expelled. <br /><br />And speaking of parties, the Legacy is coming up. It's the invitation-only Halloween party in NYC and it's rumored that Thomas -- Reed's MIA boyfriend -- will be making an appearance there. Too bad Reed isn't even close to invited. <br /><br />Life as a Billings Girl is every bit as glamorous as Reed imagined. What she didn't bargain for is the tangled web of private lies these girls weave.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11315733021438530377">This was a YA contemporary story, set at a private boarding school.<br/><br/>Reed was put in a hard position in this, and didn’t seem to be able to find her way out of it. I was glad that she did eventually work out what do though.<br/><br/>The storyline in this continued with the Billings Girl’s making Reed do stuff for them and treating her like Cinderella, we also got a bit of blackmail happening, and an exclusive party that Reed was desperate to go to. We also got a bit of romance, with a different boy this tim</span>
  <span id="freeText11315733021438530377" style="display:none">This was a YA contemporary story, set at a private boarding school.<br><br>Reed was put in a hard position in this, and didn’t seem to be able to find her way out of it. I was glad that she did eventually work out what do though.<br><br>The storyline in this continued with the Billings Girl’s making Reed do stuff for them and treating her like Cinderella, we also got a bit of blackmail happening, and an exclusive party that Reed was desperate to go to. We also got a bit of romance, with a different boy this time, although it seemed like Reed was mainly using him for what he could get her.<br><br>The ending to this was quite surprising, and was the best part of the book for me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433081147i/15047180.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>6.5 out of 10</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125498000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13248364247537847575">Oh yes, I’m officially sucked in to the Private series. Invitation Only is the second book in the Private series and now that I’m finished, I’m anxiously awaiting the arrival of book 3 at my library. I’ve already ordered the 4th book, so I can keep reading once I finish the next one.<br/><br/>Invitation Only continues the story of Reed Brennan who has just been invited by the fabulous Billings Girls to be a part of their inner circle and live in Billings Hall. Reed is excited because now, she’s in!<br/><br/>Little </span>
  <span id="freeText13248364247537847575" style="display:none">Oh yes, I’m officially sucked in to the Private series. Invitation Only is the second book in the Private series and now that I’m finished, I’m anxiously awaiting the arrival of book 3 at my library. I’ve already ordered the 4th book, so I can keep reading once I finish the next one.<br /><br />Invitation Only continues the story of Reed Brennan who has just been invited by the fabulous Billings Girls to be a part of their inner circle and live in Billings Hall. Reed is excited because now, she’s in!<br /><br />Little does she know that being asked to move into Billings Hall was just to get her closer to the Billings Girls to do their chores and be available at their every whim. Still, Reed is thrilled because she wants so badly to be popular.<br /><br />In book 1, Reed’s boyfriend Thomas goes missing. Book 2 starts off with Reed thinking about where he could possibly be and the police coming in for an investigation.<br /><br />Now that she’s a Billings girl, Reed has a new roommate: Natasha. Natasha is angry because Reed is only her new roommate because her previous roommate Leanne got kicked out of Easton Academy for “cheating” though Natasha thinks the Billings girls were behind the whole thing. Natasha blackmails Reed with incriminating photos from a party and asks her to snoop around the Billings girls rooms to find any evidence that the got Leanne kicked out.<br /><br />Boy troubles, friend troubles, and classes are not the only problem Reed has. There is an invitation only party that Reed desperately wants to go to because she thinks Thomas will be there. The Legacy party is epic in Easton history and Reed will do anything to get an invite.<br /><br />I loved this book even more than the first installment. Now that I know all of the characters and the back story, I’m intrigued to find out more about their lives and who they really are. This book kept me on the edge of my seat as there was a bit of a mystery to be solved.<br /><br />After reading the second book, I’m a certified Kate Brian fan. I love her writing style and the way she tells the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13248364247537847575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_614685374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/614685374" />
    <a title="Lady Entropy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7368944-lady-entropy"><img alt="Lady Entropy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326049487p2/7368944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/614685374?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Entropy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Entropy" href="/user/show/7368944-lady-entropy">Lady Entropy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer614685374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10595532520660586218">There is something VERY VERY disturbingly wrong with the main character.<br/><br/>She sees abuse as "friendship". Her relationship to the Billings girls is pretty much "Oooh, they're awesome, and my life sucks, thus I need to be their friend to have a bright future."<br/><br/>Wait. Scratch that.<br/><br/>Now, that is the problem. She doesn't NEED to be their friend. No, that'd actually make the book good and the character deeper. She WANTS to. Oh, sure, she moans and complains about her mom and her life back home, but most o</span>
  <span id="freeText10595532520660586218" style="display:none">There is something VERY VERY disturbingly wrong with the main character.<br /><br />She sees abuse as "friendship". Her relationship to the Billings girls is pretty much "Oooh, they're awesome, and my life sucks, thus I need to be their friend to have a bright future."<br /><br />Wait. Scratch that.<br /><br />Now, that is the problem. She doesn't NEED to be their friend. No, that'd actually make the book good and the character deeper. She WANTS to. Oh, sure, she moans and complains about her mom and her life back home, but most of the time, she sees those abusive bitches as friends. And she wants to be their friend.<br /><br />I really wish that the character started with loathing them but needing to hang out with them to get access to a good future...and slowly find their human side and starting to care for them. But nope. Reed seems to be a masochist, dead set in taking abuse after abuse. Maybe it's an american thing, I don't know -- I heard that hazing and pledge week and all sort of that stuff can be very intense and people are still glad to go through it.<br /><br />In my country, there is an incredibly old and strict university hazing tradition -- so it's not the initiations rituals that bother me. It's how the main character is a spineless chump.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10595532520660586218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_21683333" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21683333" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21683333?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-personally-by-moi">read-personally-by-moi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21683333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16118103321905429341">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>INVITATION ONLY, the second novel in the PRIVATE series, begins where we left off in the first book. Thomas went missing, one of the Billings Girls was expelled, and Reed Brennan finally moved into the dorm she had her eye on when she first came to the private school. But even though Reed was in the Billings house, that didn't exactly mean she was in the clique. <br/><br/>Turns out, the Billings Girls had a little hazing present for Reed</span>
  <span id="freeText16118103321905429341" style="display:none">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />INVITATION ONLY, the second novel in the PRIVATE series, begins where we left off in the first book. Thomas went missing, one of the Billings Girls was expelled, and Reed Brennan finally moved into the dorm she had her eye on when she first came to the private school. But even though Reed was in the Billings house, that didn't exactly mean she was in the clique. <br /><br />Turns out, the Billings Girls had a little hazing present for Reed that would keep her busy. That's right--Reed has to actually do the girls' beds every morning and clean up the dorm. Who knows exactly how long that will last. <br /><br />But that's not the only thing on Reed's mind. Her boyfriend, Thomas Pearce, had just went missing during parents' weekend. And the only possible way that she would be able to see him again is at a social event called the Legacy, held in New York City that apparently Thomas is for sure making an appearance at. The only problem is that Reed has no idea what the Legacy is--but all she is worried about is getting there. Oh, and her new roommate took compromising photos of Reed and a certain someone, and is now using it to blackmail Reed. <br /><br />From finding her boyfriend to overcoming her blackmailer to trying to officially become a Billings Girl, Reed has too much on her plate. <br /><br />It seemed like it would be hard for Kate Brian to top the first book in the PRIVATE series, which was absolutely amazing, but no worries since she does not disappoint. INVITATION ONLY was even better than the first. With even more obstacles that Reed has to face, the story literally leaves the reader at the edge of their seat. And Kate Brian ends the story with another huge cliffhanger. This series definitely tops all the other series out there. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16118103321905429341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1745684-janelle-dazzlepants?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1745684-janelle-dazzlepants?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1745684-janelle-dazzlepants?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1745684-janelle-dazzlepants?shelf=murder-mystery">murder-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer146849838&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146849838" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11656109615390136839">I take it back. If you're going to read Invitation Only expecting a murder mystery, don't bother. Nothing happens until literally the last couple of pages, and you can get away with reading those 5 pages and skipping straight to the next book. <br/><br/>As a result, much like Private I can only review Invitation Only as a piece of chick lit, and in that respect it's quite fucking boring. Despite blackmail plots, lavish parties, an enigmatic new character and final confirmation of Thomas' death, this book </span>
  <span id="freeText11656109615390136839" style="display:none">I take it back. If you're going to read Invitation Only expecting a murder mystery, don't bother. Nothing happens until literally the last couple of pages, and you can get away with reading those 5 pages and skipping straight to the next book. <br /><br />As a result, much like Private I can only review Invitation Only as a piece of chick lit, and in that respect it's quite fucking boring. Despite blackmail plots, lavish parties, an enigmatic new character and final confirmation of Thomas' death, this book felt really bloody dull. I forgave the author for a somewhat uneventful plotline in Private since I assumed she was setting the scene, but now I'm worrying that all her books are like this. For a murder mystery it's certainly light on the murder and mystery. <br /><br />I think the author is failing at something that Pretty Little Liars author Sara Shepard managed to perfect. She was able to weave teenage issues and dramas together with a huge overarching murder mystery without either element feeling like it ever played second fiddle. Obviously I've only read two books so it's not an accurate reflection of the series, but it feels like the murder mystery takes a backseat 98% of the time. If the pace doesn't pick up in the next book I am going to be seriously disappointed!<br /><br />I said in my review of Private that Reed annoyed me a little bit, but now it's escalated to me wanting to punch her through the pages. One of the things I hate most in book/film/tv show plots is when a character lies to the police to protect someone for trivial reasons, and Reed does exactly that in Invitation Only. She gets a note from Thomas saying he's in rehab, and she decides not to tell the investigating officer because it would mean that Thomas would get into trouble with his parents. Surely if your boyfriend had gone missing you'd prefer him getting into trouble with his parents to being potentially murdered?! Even though I'm certain the note was fake and could've lead the police on a wild goose chase it doesn't make me want to punch Reed any less. <br /><br />I also <i>hate</i> how she used Walt Whittaker. She lead him on at his birthday dinner and blatantly used him to get into a private party, and I think it really shows she's meant to be a Billings girl. I get that she didn't want to disappoint him on his birthday and she really hoped to see Thomas at Legacy, but I still hate her for it. The author tried to make the reader sympathetic to Reed's cause, but it didn't work. On the other hand, if the author actually did it to show Reed's gradual transformation to a vindictive Billings girl, then it totally worked. I'm a bit worried about the next few books though, because I personally can't stand bitchy main characters. I loathed the Vampire Diaries books for this reason, so Reed better redeem herself or get her ass kicked!<br /><br />Walt Whittaker was definitely an interesting character and odd addition to the story. I liked seeing how everybody falls all over him but none of the guys <i>really</i> want to be his friend. And Reed was initially attracted to him, but once they hooked up she was disgusted. I have to admit my opinions changed too, though not necessarily along with Reed's. I think he's enigmatic and I felt sorry for him for not having real friends and for being used by Reed, but then I was also disgusted by his conduct during the makeout scenes and in supporting the archaic "traditions" in the Boston restaurant. <br /><br />I'm really intrigued to see where his story goes though, because he's such an odd addition to the story. I figure the author has to have a good reason for including such a unique character, right? Aside from getting together with Constance I'd like to see him have a big role in the story, hopefully in the murder mystery! I know I'll be terribly disappointed if the author is just like 'HERE HAVE THIS WEIRD CHARACTER' *does nothing with plotarc* <br /><br />I also really like that the author included a lesbian couple in this book. A derogatory comment was made by a character in Private about it only being okay for lesbian couples to be out on campus if they were hot, and it really bothered me. Though it would've been better to not have that statement in the book in the first place, I'm glad that gay students aren't completely relegated to the sidelines. I also thought it was a cool juxtaposition to have Natasha's strict Republican parents be completely comfortable with her sexuality, and the partner being the one who can't come out. Granted we don't know anything about Leanne's backstory, but it was refreshing nonetheless.<br /><br />I <i>loved</i> the blackmail plot too. I think it was quite well-written, because everytime Reed searched the rooms I was really worried that Noelle, Ariana, Taylor or Kiran would bust in and discover her. As a reader I practically listened along with Reed for footsteps whenever she went snooping. I didn't even consider that it could've been orchestrated by them until Natasha revealed everything (which made the subsequent reveal scene with the Billings girls totally redundant). I'm so excited to see what the girls are actually hiding, because girls that can orchestrate a blackmail plot and purposely plant 'secrets' have to be hiding even juicier ones. <br /><br /><b>Overall:</b> If you enjoy the high school politics of Easton you might consider reading this book, but if you're just here for the murder mystery give it a miss. Read Private to set up the story and then read the last 5 pages of Invitation Only. You won't miss <i>anything</i>. ;]</span>
  <a data-text-id="11656109615390136839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2071726154" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2071726154" />
    <a title="Lisa Croci" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66770503-lisa-croci"><img alt="Lisa Croci" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491827436p2/66770503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Croci" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Croci" href="/user/show/66770503-lisa-croci">Lisa Croci</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2071726154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1240024072495228093">I love every book in this series, reminds me of high school days back in private school in CT. Girls only, fun times.</span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192679675?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica | Booked J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica | Booked J" href="/user/show/5392797-jessica-booked-j">Jessica | Booked J</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192679675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5004957074237542547"><a href='http://bookandbroadway.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> | <a href='http://twitter.com/bookedj' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> | <a href='http://instagram.com/jessicabeckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a><br/><br/><b>Sequels can often be a bore</b> but in the case of the second novel in the best-selling <i>Private</i> series by Kate Brian, it's even better than our introduction to Easton. <i>Invitation Only</i> picks up immediately where <i>Private</i> ended and toys with us as we grow more and more captivated to the now-luxurious everyday life of Reed Brennan. Just a bit of time she's spent at her new, ultra-exclusive boarding school, Reed has found herself as the newest member of the campus' most notoriou</span>
  <span id="freeText5004957074237542547" style="display:none"><a href="http://bookandbroadway.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/bookedj" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/jessicabeckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a><br /><br /><b>Sequels can often be a bore</b> but in the case of the second novel in the best-selling <i>Private</i> series by Kate Brian, it's even better than our introduction to Easton. <i>Invitation Only</i> picks up immediately where <i>Private</i> ended and toys with us as we grow more and more captivated to the now-luxurious everyday life of Reed Brennan. Just a bit of time she's spent at her new, ultra-exclusive boarding school, Reed has found herself as the newest member of the campus' most notorious housing department: Billings.<br /><br />The Billings Girls are everything anyone has ever dreamed to be and certainly the most sought-after dorm throughout the entire school. They're the brightest and most beautiful female students and with her newfound position amongst their ranks, Reed's future seems brighter than ever. If you ignore her missing kind-of-boyfriend Thomas Pearson, the pressure of excellence and the probability of being hazed (what is she, their maid?) by her new dorm mates before officially becoming one of their own.<br /><br />Just as Reed is finding her way around these speed bumps at her new school, it is obvious that things are just going to keep her on her toes. From the ever present affection from one of the senior boys, who insists on showering her with gifts, and with whom she has no real feelings for but her former roommate Constance does, to becoming Billings unofficial maid, to wondering where the hell Thomas is and if she should move on, to her currently roommate Natasha seemingly blackmailing her--threatening her entire future at Easton--it's obvious to say that Reed has a lot more on her plate than she'd ever expected.<br /><br />Continued: <a href="http://bookandbroadway.blogspot.com/2016/11/invitation-only-by-kate-brian-rating.html" rel="nofollow noopener">BOOKEDJ </a></span>

<div id="review_96950902" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96950902" />
    <a title="Noa Meshorer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3127385-noa-meshorer"><img alt="Noa Meshorer" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96950902?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Noa Meshorer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Noa Meshorer" href="/user/show/3127385-noa-meshorer">Noa Meshorer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3127385-noa-meshorer?shelf=8th-grade-ir-books-chris-mc-cloud">8th-grade-ir-books-chris-mc-cloud</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96950902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9610954849286452405"><u>Invitation only</u> , is the second book of the Private series. Reed is now a Billing girl and is accepted to be part of the group but she still has to do tasks for them in order to fully belong to their clique. Thomas disappearing is starting to make Reed and the others worried and an investigation is taking place in the whole school. A prestigious party named the "Legacy" is coming up soon and Reed is hoping to be invited because she heard that Thomas never misses it. Her only chance to go to this</span>
  <span id="freeText9610954849286452405" style="display:none"><u>Invitation only</u> , is the second book of the Private series. Reed is now a Billing girl and is accepted to be part of the group but she still has to do tasks for them in order to fully belong to their clique. Thomas disappearing is starting to make Reed and the others worried and an investigation is taking place in the whole school. A prestigious party named the "Legacy" is coming up soon and Reed is hoping to be invited because she heard that Thomas never misses it. Her only chance to go to this party is by being invited by a boy named Whit who is in love with her. Throughout the book, Reed is discovering some secrets about the Billing girls. There is a tragic event that will shift Reed's life at Easton Academy.<br /><br />I can make a connection to the movie American beauty. It reminds me of the main concept in the movie where life seems perfect and ideal on the outside but behind this facade there are hidden ugly secrets. As for the Billing girls and the school, behind the all perfect, rich and powerful image there are human weaknesses. In fact it is happening everywhere in our society where people are creating a false image of themselves to prevent judging and they prefer to show power than being honest.<br /><br />I rated this book 5 stars. It is as the first one very intriguing and suspenseful. The ends are always surprising. I would recommend this book to teenagers who like books with a mix of drama, love and suspension.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9610954849286452405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11720579115164316474" style="display:none">Reed Brennan is now part of the Billings Girls but her troubles are far from over. A handsy, bordering stalkerish guy enters the picture. Her new roommate Natalie blackmails her with incriminating photos. The story follows on seamlessly from Private. Majority of the events that occurred in the story were quite pointless <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Really? The bitchiness and the scandals of the girls were still the main focus of the story, which makes it interesting! <div id="review_2336766335" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2336766335" />
    <a title="Abby Vaughn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69913430-abby-vaughn"><img alt="Abby Vaughn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551842921p2/69913430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2336766335?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby Vaughn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby Vaughn" href="/user/show/69913430-abby-vaughn">Abby Vaughn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2336766335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2721903700801275545">I got 60 pages in and has to stop. Honestly, Reed became even more desperate and needy in this one. The Billings Girls literally make her clean their whole house and she just does it to please them even though she ends up being exhausted. But that’s what it takes to fit in with them, am I right ? <br/><br/>Reed became the biggest pushover I’ve ever seen in my life and she had no backbone at all !! She does anything to please these one dimensional stuck up Billings Girls and the worst part is, she does it </span>
  <span id="freeText2721903700801275545" style="display:none">I got 60 pages in and has to stop. Honestly, Reed became even more desperate and needy in this one. The Billings Girls literally make her clean their whole house and she just does it to please them even though she ends up being exhausted. But that’s what it takes to fit in with them, am I right ? <br /><br />Reed became the biggest pushover I’ve ever seen in my life and she had no backbone at all !! She does anything to please these one dimensional stuck up Billings Girls and the worst part is, she does it like it’s second nature to her. She’s not original or unique and she’s quite bland. I honestly don’t think I’ll even consider finishing the series because of these stupid characters- not one of them is even remotely likeable or redeemable. <br /><br />My advice ? Don’t waste your time and just read spoilers - it’s better than having to suffer through this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2721903700801275545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

This book is a real guilty pleasure. &amp; in my opinion, even better than Gossip Girl.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IxOcpMDnGkR5eGgVJ7DijspB0xKnZw6XjqHKpHKT5VfwkzXyIZcFBkg944MBmtT/P4Nd7v+tsalWjWqhFvGQ1w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dmb2bMentMnIa3c+2fCTymXvJVrtWbahxQXPt6WljYql5l86Jteri/ku/Kj/2qW7kC2rprWTCZ8dKW+ywcf4Cg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Then, miraculously, the dreaded move is cancelled, and things seem to be getting better -- at least until 17-year-old Robbie decides to break up with Georgia because he\'s bothered by the difference in their ages. \n\nBorrowing freely from her mum\'s closet and advice books, even as she\'s steadfastly discounting everything her mum says, a crushed but determined Georgia comes up with a scheme to win Robbie back. As usual, nothing goes as planned, and life is further complicated by Georgia\'s temperamental cat, Angus (who\'s having a few amorous leanings of his own), and her baby sister, Libby, whose fascination with (and lack of control over) her bodily functions leads to several intriguing mishaps. This Georgia\'s-eye view of teenage life is wonderfully egocentric and side-splittingly funny. And despite the occasional language barrier (a glossary of terms is provided in the back of the book), Georgia\'s thoughts and experiences will prove universally recognizable to anyone who is, or has
